♠ Polity has obligation to other polity or group ♣ present ♥ Sassanids discontinue tribute payment to Byzantines? "The Byzantine chronicler Priscus mentions the 'Kidarite Huns' for the first time in 456 as adversaries of the Sasanian king Yazdgird II (438-457), who had discontinued a tribute paid by his predecessors to Iran’s eastern neighbours (Exc. De Leg. Rom. 8, ed. Blockley 1983, pp. 336-7)."[1,236] Tribute to the Hephthalites under Balash (484-488 CE).[1,237]
♠ Polity receives obligatory payment from other polity or group ♣ present ♥ In the Early Sasanian period vassals paid tribute.[1,238] Apparently between the years 330 and 340 the Kushan lands in the northern part of the Kushan Empire were under the suzerainty of the Sasanians, but we know nothing about the form of this dependence."[1,239]

Taxation[edit]

♠ Degree of taxation ♣ ♥ Khusrau I (later Sassanid period) ordered lands to be measured, fixed tax per griv (1/10 hectare) according to what was grown. Khusrau (later Sassanid period) demanded "all persons between the ages of 20 and 50, except nobles, soldiers and priests ... to pay the poll tax, whose amount ranged from 12 drachms (Arabic dirhams) to 4 drachms, according to wealth."[1,240] "Under the Sasanids, the Silk Route flourished. The government controlled trade and imposed heavy taxes on all goods passing through its lands."[1,241][MAJIDBENAM_BR]"The seven families certainly exercised authority over entire provinces where the peasants were obliged to pay taxes to them in addition to the taxes demanded by the royal treasury."[1,242] Was this still true after the reforms of Khusrau I in the early sixth century?[MAJIDBENAM_BR]Taxes are imposed on:
♠ Land ♣ present ♥ At the time the Arabs took over in the seventh century they retained the Sasanid taxation system which included a land and poll tax.[1,243]
♠ Property ♣ ♥
♠ People ♣ inferred absent ♥ Khusrau I (later Sassanid period) demanded "all persons between the ages of 20 and 50, except nobles, soldiers and priests ... to pay the poll tax, whose amount ranged from 12 drachms (Arabic dirhams) to 4 drachms, according to wealth."[1,244] Khusrau I's reform of the tax system occurred in the sixth century so presumably there was no poll tax in this earlier period.
♠ Trade ♣ present ♥ "Under the Sasanids, the Silk Route flourished. The government controlled trade and imposed heavy taxes on all goods passing through its lands."[1,245]
♠ Income ♣ ♥
♠ Production ♣ present ♥ Arab historian al-Tabari claimed that "farmers had no right to harvest crops or gather fruit from their garden before the arrival of the tax collector; the long wait meant that their produce was frequently wasted."[1,246] In the sixth century this situation was reformed by Khusrau I's new fiscal system.[1,247][MAJIDBENAM_BR]Taxes are imposed by:
♠ executive or ruling elite ♣ present ♥ "The great tax reform of Khusrau I marked a turning point in the Sasanian state administration. For the first time, the power of the landed nobility was restricted and all the taxes were in the hands of the king."[1,248] After Khusrau I's (later Sassanid period) reform of the tax system "Supervision of the payment of taxes into the royal treasury was undertaken by the hamarkar (accountant)".[1,249] After Khusrau I's (later Sassanid period) reform of the tax system "The taxes were collected according to the administrative sub-divisions of the country from village up to province, with the officer in charge of a province being responsible for overall supervision and the tax in each city being paid to the judge of that city."[1,250] Taxes were imposed by the king but it wasn't until Khusrau I's reforms in the sixth century that the system was centralized.
♠ local elites ♣ inferred present ♥ Peasants were bound to their village community that was liable for its members' duties (taxes and corvees)."[1,251] "The great tax reform of Khusrau I marked a turning point in the Sasanian state administration. For the first time, the power of the landed nobility was restricted and all the taxes were in the hands of the king."[1,252] After Khusrau I's (later Sassanid period) reform of the tax system "Supervision of the payment of taxes into the royal treasury was undertaken by the hamarkar (accountant)".[1,253] After Khusrau I's (later Sassanid period) reform of the tax system "The taxes were collected according to the administrative sub-divisions of the country from village up to province, with the officer in charge of a province being responsible for overall supervision and the tax in each city being paid to the judge of that city."[1,254] Khusrau I's reforms which centralized the tax system and put the collection of taxes in the hands of officials occurred in the sixth century. Before his time tax collection was therefore less centralized; apparently under the control of the landed nobility.
♠ state officials ♣ inferred absent ♥ "The great tax reform of Khusrau I marked a turning point in the Sasanian state administration. For the first time, the power of the landed nobility was restricted and all the taxes were in the hands of the king."[1,255] After Khusrau I's (later Sassanid period) reform of the tax system "Supervision of the payment of taxes into the royal treasury was undertaken by the hamarkar (accountant)".[1,256] After Khusrau I's (later Sassanid period) reform of the tax system "The taxes were collected according to the administrative sub-divisions of the country from village up to province, with the officer in charge of a province being responsible for overall supervision and the tax in each city being paid to the judge of that city."[1,257] Khusrau I's reforms which centralized the tax system and put the collection of taxes in the hands of officials occurred in the sixth century. Before his time tax collection was therefore less centralized; apparently under the control of the landed nobility.[MAJIDBENAM_BR]Type of taxes paid:
♠ Staple ♣ present ♥ In rural areas wages and often taxes were paid in kind.[1,258]
♠ Labor ♣ ♥
♠ Currency ♣ inferred present ♥ "Under the Sasanids, the Silk Route flourished. The government controlled trade and imposed heavy taxes on all goods passing through its lands."[1,259] "Sasanid coins found in ports of southern China, and others discovered in northeastern China, indicate trade with Fars by the Silk Route by sea."[1,260] coins were used in international trade in this era so it is very likely taxes could be paid in currency.

Wages and Costs[edit]

♠ Wages ♣ ♥ There was "a relatively strong and wealthy bourgeois class" which included merchants and "heads of industrial workshops".[1,261]
♠ staple cost of principal source of carbohydrates ♣ ♥
♠ Top fortune ♣ ♥
♠ Other wealth distribution ♣ ♥ Late 4th century inequality was such that priest Mazdak "came up with the idea of redistribution of the two basic necessities of life, accumulated in the hands of a few: material goods (lands and/or granaies) and wives in the harems. The king of the day, Kavad (AD 488-531), pressed upon from all sides (by unruly aristocracy within the country, by the nomads, the mountain peoples and the Byzantines from without) connived in the plan: and the reform began to be implemented."[1,262] Later "the priesthood, supported by the crown prince, Khusraw, persuaded the king to stop the Mazdaic redistribution which, having lasted about 25 years, achieved quite a few of its goals. The Council of the Magi summond by the king, condemned Mazdak as a heretic and the crown prince arranged the execution of Mazdak and many of his followers. Previous property rights were painfully restored."[1,263] "As with the Parthians, the economy was based on agriculture. Revenue increased during the Sassanid period led gradually to a fairer redistribution of goods."[1,264][MAJIDBENAM_BR] ♠ Dedicated police force ♣ present ♥ Specialist law enforcement officials. Alexander the Great c330 BCE with the Macedonian conquest of Persia introduced the Greek Polis system which organized the law and order in the cities. "It is very likely that the term police in Western languages has its source in the Greek notion of Polis.” Under this system "An official named Epistat, appointed by the monarchy, oversaw the manner in which the Polis performed its duties. ... The Shahrik and the Dayhlik were two additional administrative and governing bodies whose development goes to the time of the Sassanid Empire (Kusha 2000). The Shahrik was responsible for law enforcement and security matters pertaining to cities, whereas the Dayhik performed these duties in villages. It is logical to assume that these order-imposing institutions borrowed legal and administrative concepts and technical know-how from their predecessors, for instance, from the Hellenistic institution of Polis mentioned above.”[1,265] From the 4th century: "religions communities were organized as legal corporations owning property; maintaining courts; regulating marriages, divorces and inheritances; and through their chiefs, holding responsibility to the state for taxes and discipline."</ref>(Lapidus 2012, 16) Lapidus, I M. 2012. Islamic Societies to the Nineteenth Century: A Global History. Cambridge University Press. Cambridge.</ref>
♠ Police levels ♣ 4 ♥ 1. King 2. Provincial governor 3. Sharik (city) or Dayhlik (village) 4. Policeman (in city)? Alexander the Great c330 BCE with the Macedonian conquest of Persia introduced the Greek Polis system which organized the law and order in the cities. "It is very likely that the term police in Western languages has its source in the Greek notion of Polis.” Under this system "An official named Epistat, appointed by the monarchy, oversaw the manner in which the Polis performed its duties. ... The Shahrik and the Dayhlik were two additional administrative and governing bodies whose development goes to the time of the Sassanid Empire (Kusha 2000). The Shahrik was responsible for law enforcement and security matters pertaining to cities, whereas the Dayhik performed these duties in villages. It is logical to assume that these order-imposing institutions borrowed legal and administrative concepts and technical know-how from their predecessors, for instance, from the Hellenistic institution of Polis mentioned above.”[1,266] From the 4th century: "religions communities were organized as legal corporations owning property; maintaining courts; regulating marriages, divorces and inheritances; and through their chiefs, holding responsibility to the state for taxes and discipline."</ref>(Lapidus 2012, 16) Lapidus, I M. 2012. Islamic Societies to the Nineteenth Century: A Global History. Cambridge University Press. Cambridge.</ref>
♠ Proscriptions of elites and or property ♣ ♥ Use of the state to repress or purge rival elite groups.
♠ Corporal punishment by the state ♣ ♥
♠ Military control over independent or semi-independent vassal states ♣ present ♥ Semi-independent vassal kingdoms (Merv, Kerman, Sakastan, Adiabene, Iberia, Makran, Mesene, Kushanshahr and Armenia).[1,267]
